# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed the task. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've identified all the Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the consumer group coordinator's state machine, including the Join, Sync, and Rebalance states and their transitions. The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Findings:

**Four State Machine Implementations:**

1. **Classic Group State Machine**: EMPTY → PREPARING_REBALANCE (Join) → COMPLETING_REBALANCE (Sync) → STABLE
2. **Modern Consumer Group State Machine**: EMPTY → ASSIGNING → RECONCILING → STABLE (updated protocol)
3. **Share Group State Machine**: EMPTY → STABLE (simplified for share consumers)
4. **Streams Group State Machine**: EMPTY → NOT_READY → ASSIGNING → RECONCILING → STABLE

**Core Files Located:**
- `ClassicGroupState.java` - Enum with join/sync/rebalance state transitions
- `ClassicGroup.java` - Group manager enforcing state transitions
- `ConsumerGroup.java` - Modern group with ASSIGNING/RECONCILING states
- `GroupMetadataManager.java` - Central coordinator handling all state transitions
- Supporting member and modern group base classes

All 17 core files have been documented in the answer file with detailed explanation of how the Join (recruiting members), Sync (distributing assignments), and Rebalance (steady state) phases work through the state machines.

The implementation spans both server-side coordinators and client-side membership managers.\\n\\n**Classic Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.classic):**\\n\\nThe ClassicGroupState enum (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java) defines five states with specific valid transitions:\\n\\n- EMPTY: Initial state where the group has no members. Transitions to PREPARING_REBALANCE when members join.\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE (Join Phase): Group waits for members to join within a timeout period. Members send JoinGroup requests. Transitions to COMPLETING_REBALANCE when a leader is elected or timeout occurs.\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE (Sync Phase): Group waits for leader to compute assignments and members to send SyncGroup requests. Transitions to STABLE when all members have synced.\\n- STABLE: Active rebalance state where members can fetch and consume with current assignments. Transitions back to PREPARING_REBALANCE if a member fails, leaves, or updates metadata.\\n- DEAD: Final state before cleanup. Can transition from any other state.\\n\\nThe ClassicGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroup.java) manages the group state and enforces valid transitions. ClassicGroupMember (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupMember.java) tracks individual member state with awaitingJoinFuture and awaitingSyncFuture for coordination.\\n\\n**Modern Consumer Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.modern.consumer):**\\n\\nThe ConsumerGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroup.java) implements an updated state machine with states:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members in the group.\\n- ASSIGNING: Group is computing target assignments for all members using partition assignors.\\n- RECONCILING: Members are reconciling to their target assignments (pulling assignments and revoking previous partitions).\\n- STABLE: All members have completed reconciliation and are in steady state.\\n- DEAD: Group is marked for deletion.\\n\\nThe transitions flow as: EMPTY \u2192 ASSIGNING \u2192 RECONCILING \u2192 STABLE, with the ability to return to ASSIGNING from STABLE when metadata changes trigger rebalancing. ConsumerGroupMember (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroupMember.java) manages member-specific state.\\n\\n**Share Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.modern.share):**\\n\\nThe ShareGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/share/ShareGroup.java) implements a simpler state machine:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members.\\n- STABLE: Members are actively consuming.\\n- DEAD: Group being removed.\\n- UNKNOWN: Initial/fallback state.\\n\\n**Streams Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.streams):**\\n\\nThe StreamsGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/streams/StreamsGroup.java) implements:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members.\\n- NOT_READY: Group cannot assign tasks (topology not ready).\\n- ASSIGNING: Computing task assignments.\\n- RECONCILING: Members reconciling task assignments.\\n- STABLE: All members have tasks assigned and reconciled.\\n- DEAD: Group being removed.\\n\\n**State Transition Orchestration:**\\n\\nThe GroupMetadataManager class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadataManager.java) is the central coordinator managing all state transitions. It handles JoinGroup requests (initiating rebalance), SyncGroup requests (completing rebalance), heartbeats (maintaining stable state), and member departures (triggering new rebalance).\\n\\n**Client-Side State Enums:**\\n\\nClient-side representations are provided in:\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/ClassicGroupState.java\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/ConsumerGroupState.java (deprecated)\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/GroupState.java (unified enum)\\n\\n**Member State Management:**\\n\\nThe MemberState enum (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/MemberState.java) tracks individual member reconciliation states separate from group-level states, enabling fine-grained tracking of member progress through assignment reconciliation (UNJOINED \u2192 JOINING \u2192 STABLE \u2192 RECONCILING \u2192 ACKNOWLEDGING \u2192 LEAVING \u2192 UNSUBSCRIBED).\\n\\nThe state machines implement the Kafka rebalancing protocol with Join (PREPARING_REBALANCE in classic, ASSIGNING in modern), Sync (COMPLETING_REBALANCE in classic, RECONCILING in modern), and Stable (STABLE across all types) phases, ensuring coordinated group membership changes and assignment distribution.\"\n}\n",

The implementation spans both server-side coordinators and client-side membership managers.\\n\\n**Classic Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.classic):**\\n\\nThe ClassicGroupState enum (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupState.java) defines five states with specific valid transitions:\\n\\n- EMPTY: Initial state where the group has no members. Transitions to PREPARING_REBALANCE when members join.\\n- PREPARING_REBALANCE (Join Phase): Group waits for members to join within a timeout period. Members send JoinGroup requests. Transitions to COMPLETING_REBALANCE when a leader is elected or timeout occurs.\\n- COMPLETING_REBALANCE (Sync Phase): Group waits for leader to compute assignments and members to send SyncGroup requests. Transitions to STABLE when all members have synced.\\n- STABLE: Active rebalance state where members can fetch and consume with current assignments. Transitions back to PREPARING_REBALANCE if a member fails, leaves, or updates metadata.\\n- DEAD: Final state before cleanup. Can transition from any other state.\\n\\nThe ClassicGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroup.java) manages the group state and enforces valid transitions. ClassicGroupMember (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/classic/ClassicGroupMember.java) tracks individual member state with awaitingJoinFuture and awaitingSyncFuture for coordination.\\n\\n**Modern Consumer Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.modern.consumer):**\\n\\nThe ConsumerGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroup.java) implements an updated state machine with states:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members in the group.\\n- ASSIGNING: Group is computing target assignments for all members using partition assignors.\\n- RECONCILING: Members are reconciling to their target assignments (pulling assignments and revoking previous partitions).\\n- STABLE: All members have completed reconciliation and are in steady state.\\n- DEAD: Group is marked for deletion.\\n\\nThe transitions flow as: EMPTY \u2192 ASSIGNING \u2192 RECONCILING \u2192 STABLE, with the ability to return to ASSIGNING from STABLE when metadata changes trigger rebalancing. ConsumerGroupMember (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/consumer/ConsumerGroupMember.java) manages member-specific state.\\n\\n**Share Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.modern.share):**\\n\\nThe ShareGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/share/ShareGroup.java) implements a simpler state machine:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members.\\n- STABLE: Members are actively consuming.\\n- DEAD: Group being removed.\\n- UNKNOWN: Initial/fallback state.\\n\\n**Streams Group State Machine (org.apache.kafka.coordinator.group.streams):**\\n\\nThe StreamsGroup class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/streams/StreamsGroup.java) implements:\\n\\n- EMPTY: No members.\\n- NOT_READY: Group cannot assign tasks (topology not ready).\\n- ASSIGNING: Computing task assignments.\\n- RECONCILING: Members reconciling task assignments.\\n- STABLE: All members have tasks assigned and reconciled.\\n- DEAD: Group being removed.\\n\\n**State Transition Orchestration:**\\n\\nThe GroupMetadataManager class (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadataManager.java) is the central coordinator managing all state transitions. It handles JoinGroup requests (initiating rebalance), SyncGroup requests (completing rebalance), heartbeats (maintaining stable state), and member departures (triggering new rebalance).\\n\\n**Client-Side State Enums:**\\n\\nClient-side representations are provided in:\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/ClassicGroupState.java\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/ConsumerGroupState.java (deprecated)\\n- clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/GroupState.java (unified enum)\\n\\n**Member State Management:**\\n\\nThe MemberState enum (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/modern/MemberState.java) tracks individual member reconciliation states separate from group-level states, enabling fine-grained tracking of member progress through assignment reconciliation (UNJOINED \u2192 JOINING \u2192 STABLE \u2192 RECONCILING \u2192 ACKNOWLEDGING \u2192 LEAVING \u2192 UNSUBSCRIBED).\\n\\nThe state machines implement the Kafka rebalancing protocol with Join (PREPARING_REBALANCE in classic, ASSIGNING in modern), Sync (COMPLETING_REBALANCE in classic, RECONCILING in modern), and Stable (STABLE across all types) phases, ensuring coordinated group membership changes and assignment distribution.\"\n}\n",
